## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the rate of change of concentration in a chemical reaction, which is a fundamental concept in chemical kinetics. The relationship between concentration and time is expected to be non-linear, possibly exhibiting saturation or growth.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- zeroth order kinetics: rate = c0 (constant rate, no dependence on concentration)
- first order kinetics: rate = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- second order kinetics: rate = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to concentration squared)
- third order kinetics: rate = c0 * A**3 (rate proportional to concentration cubed)
- sigmoidal growth: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (concentration-dependent rate with saturation)
- monod kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (concentration-dependent rate with saturation and cooperativity)
- linlog kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + log(A)) (concentration-dependent rate with a linear-logarithmic term)
- mass action law: rate = c0 * [A]**c1 * [B]**c2 (rate proportional to concentrations of reactants A and B)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: rate = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzymatic reaction kinetics with saturation)
- Hill equation: rate = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (cooperative binding with sigmoidal behavior)
- logistic growth: dA_dt = c0 * A * (1 - A/c1) (population growth with carrying capacity)
- SIMEmployed kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c2) (enzymatic reaction kinetics with cooperativity and saturation)
- double-exponential growth: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * exp(c2*t) (concentration-dependent growth with exponential time dependence)
- power-law growth: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (concentration-dependent growth with power-law time dependence)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- concentration-dependent rate â†’ Rational fraction A/(c1+A), or variable products A*y
- saturation effects â†’ Sigmoidal function A/(c1+A), or max(A-c,0)
- growth/decay â†’ exp(c*t), or power-law growth A**c1 * t**c2
- coupling/cross effects â†’ Variable products A*y, or power-law coupling A**c1 * y**c2
